A versioned gRPC streaming\\n228:     protocol with support for ACK/NACK is provided by xDS; this is known as the\\n229:     xDS transport protocol (xDS-TP). xDS configuration resources can also be\\n230:     delivered on other transports, e.g. HTTP or filesystem, with some\\n231: \",\"endLine\":231,\"startLine\":222},{\"content\":\"234: \\n235: * The xDS APIs are directionally client and server neutral. While many aspects\\n236:   of the APIs reflect the history of their origin as Envoy's control plane APIs,\\n237:   API decisions going forward should reflect the principle of client neutrality.\\n238: \\n239: * The xDS APIs are expressed canonically as [Proto3](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/proto3).\\n240:   Both JSON and YAML are also supported formats, with the standard JSON-proto3\\n241:   conversion used during client configuration ingestion.\\n242: \\n243: * xDS APIs are eventual consistency first. For example, if RDS references a\\n244:   cluster that has not yet been supplied by CDS, it should be silently ignored\\n245: \",\"endLine\":245,\"startLine\":234},{\"content\":\"250: \\n251: * The API is primarily intended for machine generation and consumption. It is\\n252:   expected that the management server is responsible for mapping higher level\\n253:   configuration concepts to API responses. Similarly, static configuration\\n254:   fragments may be generated by templating tools, etc. With that consideration,\\n255:   we also aim to have API artifacts readable by humans for debugging and\\n256:   understanding applied configuration. This implies that APIs do not have to\\n257:   have ergonomics as the main driver, but should still be reasonable to read by\\n258:   humans. API shepherds are responsible for the execution of the xDS\\n85: day-to-day and guiding xDS implementation changes. A versioned gRPC streaming\n228:     protocol with support for ACK/NACK is provided by xDS; this is known as the\n229:     xDS transport protocol (xDS-TP). xDS configuration resources can also be\n230:     delivered on other transports, e.g. HTTP or filesystem, with some\n231: ","endLine":231,"startLine":222},{"content":"234: \n235: * The xDS APIs are directionally client and server neutral. While many aspects\n236:   of the APIs reflect the history of their origin as Envoy's control plane APIs,\n237:   API decisions going forward should reflect the principle of client neutrality.\n238: \n239: * The xDS APIs are expressed canonically as [Proto3](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/proto3).\n240:   Both JSON and YAML are also supported formats, with the standard JSON-proto3\n241:   conversion used during client configuration ingestion.\n242: \n243: * xDS APIs are eventual consistency first. Type URL to Service Mapping (source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.cc/h)\\n\\nThis file implements the critical `buildTypeUrlToServiceMap()` function which creates a reverse mapping from resource type URLs to v3 service methods. It:\\n- Explicitly enumerates all v3 services (RouteDiscoveryService, SecretDiscoveryService, etc.)\\n- Extracts resource type URLs from service annotations\\n- Maps each type URL to three service methods: SotW gRPC, Delta gRPC, and REST\\n- Provides functions like `sotwGrpcMethod()`, `deltaGrpcMethod()`, and `restMethod()` to retrieve the appropriate service method for a given type URL\\n\\nThe code explicitly handles only v3 services, but the mapping is used by the subscription factory to route requests appropriately.\\n\\n#### 3. It:\\n- Analyzes the `ConfigSource` to determine the subscription type (ADS, gRPC, REST, Filesystem)\\n- For ADS subscriptions, calls `subscriptionOverAdsGrpcMux()`\\n- Validates the API configuration source and creates appropriate subscription objects\\n- The factory detects API version through `resource_api_version` and `transport_api_version` fields in the ConfigSource\\n\\n#### 4. ADS gRPC Mux Implementations\\n\\nThere are multiple ADS implementations supporting different subscription state protocols:\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Legacy):\\n- The original ADS implementation supporting SotW (State-of-the-World) protocol\\n- `onDiscoveryResponse()` handles v3 DiscoveryResponse messages\\n- `sendDiscoveryRequest()` sends v3 DiscoveryRequest messages\\n- Uses the `apiStateFor()` method to manage per-type-url state\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Unified):\\n- Newer unified implementation that can handle both SotW and Delta protocols\\n- Implements the abstraction with template parameters for different subscription state factories\\n- Validates local node information through `Config::Utility::checkLocalInfo(\\\"ads\\\", ...)`\\n- Creates appropriate subscription state objects through the factory\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/new_grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Delta-focused):\\n- Optimized for the Delta protocol\\n- Handles `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` directly\\n- Implements `onDiscoveryResponse()` for delta-specific processing\\n- Manages resource subscriptions and unsubscriptions\\n\\n#### 5. Watch Management (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.cc/h)\\n\\nManages the mapping between resource names and subscription callbacks, supporting dynamic addition and removal of watches for resource updates.\\n\\n### Dual-Version Support Architecture\\n\\nThe system implements dual-version support through:\\n\\n1. **Configuration-Time Version Selection**: The API version is determined from the ConfigSource protobuf message during subscription creation\\n\\n2. **Type URL Routing**: The `type_to_endpoint` module maps resource type URLs (which may refer to v2 types like \\\"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.Cluster\\\") to v3 service methods\\n\\n3. **Wire Protocol Standardization**: All internal communication uses v3 protobuf messages (DiscoveryRequest, DiscoveryResponse) regardless of the input API version\\n\\n4. **Deprecation Warning System**: When v2 transport API version is detected, the system logs warnings to encourage migration to v3\\n\\n### default)\\n\\nThe ADS gRPC server implementation in grpc_mux_impl.cc and its variants handle the dual-version subscription management through proper abstraction and state management, allowing seamless through a sophisticated abstraction layer in the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server implementation. The system supports both the deprecated v2 API and the current v3 API, with proper version detection and handling.\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n#### 1. API Version Handling (source/common/config/)\\n\\n**api_version.h**: Defines the `API_NO_BOOST` macro used throughout the codebase to control API version enforcement, allowing specific code to force usage of v2 API when needed.\\n\\n**utility.h/cc**: Contains critical API version validation logic. The `getVersionStringFromApiVersion()` function converts the API version enum to string representation. Most importantly, it includes deprecation checking that logs warnings when xDS v2 transport API version is detected. The code shows that:\\n- V2 xDS transport protocol is deprecated and triggers a warning\\n- The system checks if `transport_api_version` is set to anything other than AUTO or V3\\n- When deprecated V2 is detected, it logs a message indicating v2 has been removed and directs users to documentation\\n\\n#### 2. Type URL to Service Mapping (source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.cc/h)\\n\\nThis file implements the critical `buildTypeUrlToServiceMap()` function which creates a reverse mapping from resource type URLs to v3 service methods. It:\\n- Explicitly enumerates all v3 services (RouteDiscoveryService, SecretDiscoveryService, etc.)\\n- Extracts resource type URLs from service annotations\\n- Maps each type URL to three service methods: SotW gRPC, Delta gRPC, and REST\\n- Provides functions like `sotwGrpcMethod()`, `deltaGrpcMethod()`, and `restMethod()` to retrieve the appropriate service method for a given type URL\\n\\nThe code explicitly handles only v3 services, but the mapping is used by the subscription factory to route requests appropriately.\\n\\n#### 3. Subscription Factory (source/common/config/subscription_factory_impl.cc/h)\\n\\nThe `SubscriptionFactoryImpl::subscriptionFromConfigSource()` method is the entry point for all subscription creation. It:\\n- Analyzes the `ConfigSource` to determine the subscription type (ADS, gRPC, REST, Filesystem)\\n- For ADS subscriptions, calls `subscriptionOverAdsGrpcMux()`\\n- Validates the API configuration source and creates appropriate subscription objects\\n- The factory detects API version through `resource_api_version` and `transport_api_version` fields in the ConfigSource\\n\\n#### 4. ADS gRPC Mux Implementations\\n\\nThere are multiple ADS implementations supporting different subscription state protocols:\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Legacy):\\n- The original ADS implementation supporting SotW (State-of-the-World) protocol\\n- `onDiscoveryResponse()` handles v3 DiscoveryResponse messages\\n- `sendDiscoveryRequest()` sends v3 DiscoveryRequest messages\\n- Uses the `apiStateFor()` method to manage per-type-url state\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Unified):\\n- Newer unified implementation that can handle both SotW and Delta protocols\\n- Implements the abstraction with template parameters for different subscription state factories\\n- Validates local node information through `Config::Utility::checkLocalInfo(\\\"ads\\\", ...)`\\n- Creates appropriate subscription state objects through the factory\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/new_grpc_mux_impl.cc/h** (Delta-focused):\\n- Optimized for the Delta protocol\\n- Handles `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` directly\\n- Implements `onDiscoveryResponse()` for delta-specific processing\\n- Manages resource subscriptions and unsubscriptions\\n\\n#### 5. Subscription State Management\\n\\nThe subscription state classes handle the protocol-specific logic:\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.cc/h**:\\n- Manages SotW subscription state using v3 DiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryResponse\\n- Builds the next discovery request based on current subscription state\\n- Handles resource version tracking\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.cc/h**:\\n- Manages Delta subscription state using v3 DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\n- Tracks resource subscriptions/unsubscriptions\\n- Manages resource versions efficiently\\n\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/delta_subscription_state.cc/h** and **source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_impl.cc/h**:\\n- Support for individual subscriptions over ADS\\n- Handle pause/resume of subscriptions\\n- Watch management for resource updates\\n\\n#### 6. Watch Management (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.cc/h)\\n\\nManages the mapping between resource names and subscription callbacks, supporting dynamic addition and removal of watches for resource updates.\\n\\n### Dual-Version Support Architecture\\n\\nThe system implements dual-version support through:\\n\\n1. **Configuration-Time Version Selection**: The API version is determined from the ConfigSource protobuf message during subscription creation\\n\\n2. **Type URL Routing**: The `type_to_endpoint` module maps resource type URLs (which may refer to v2 types like \\\"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.Cluster\\\") to v3 service methods\\n\\n3. **Wire Protocol Standardization**: All internal communication uses v3 protobuf messages (DiscoveryRequest, DiscoveryResponse) regardless of the input API version\\n\\n4. **Deprecation Warning System**: When v2 transport API version is detected, the system logs warnings to encourage migration to v3\\n\\n### Test Evidence\\n\\n**test/integration/ads_integration_test.cc** contains:\\n- Test `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST(RejectV2TransportConfigByDefault)` that validates v2 transport version rejection\\n- Configuration of resource_api_version and transport_api_version in test setup\\n- Demonstration of ADS message handling with v3 DiscoveryResponse\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\nThe xDS v2 to v3 API handling in Envoy is implemented through a sophisticated three-layer architecture:\\n1. **Configuration layer** that detects and validates API versions from ConfigSource messages\\n2. **Type mapping layer** that translates resource type URLs to appropriate service methods\\n3. **Protocol layer** that uses standardized v3 messages internally while supporting configuration of v2 (now deprecated and rejected by default)\\n\\nThe ADS gRPC server implementation in grpc_mux_impl.cc and its variants handle the dual-version subscription management through proper abstraction and state management, allowing seamless handling of both old v2 and current v3 API versions during the migration period.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
